asked the Minister of Mahaweli, Agriculture, Irrigation and Rural Development and Minister of Internal Trade, Food Security and Consumer Welfare and State Minister of Defence:

(a) Will he inform this House-

(i) the number of drug raids carried out;

(ii) the number of persons taken into custody for offenses related to drugs; and

(iii) the value of drugs seized;

in Kandy District during the past two years, separately in respect of each year?

(b) Will he submit to this House a list comprising of drugs which have been identified as illegal substances and the names of the countries from which they enter to Sri Lanka?

(c) Will he also inform this House-

(i) whether he is aware of the fact that Gampola and surrounding areas belonging to Kandy District have been a drug distribution hub for a while now and that the aforesaid distribution network continues to function powerfully, targeting school children and the youth; and

(ii) whether steps will be taken to capture these drug traffickers expeditiously and eliminate the drug menace from this area?

р╖Щр╢╕р╢╕ р╢н""р╖Ар╢║ р╢нр╖Аoр╢╗р╢з" р╖А:р╢░р╢▒р╢║ ┬Ьр╖Ар╖Щр╖Д" р╖Щр╢┤┬С#р╢║ р╢З+┬К р╢╗р╖Щp -Uр╢║ |р╢║р╖П"р╢╕р╢Ъ р╢Ър╢╗р╢▒ р╢Жр╢║р╢нр╢▒ Cр╢╢р╢│р╖А р╢╕р╖Д р╢вр╢▒р╢нр╖Пр╖Ар╖ЩV р╢ЗU р╖Бр╖Кр╖Ар╖Пр╖Гр╢║ ┬╣р╢│р╖Ар╖Р┬┤р╖Щ. р╢Ер╖Ар╢пр╖Пр╢▒р╢╕e р╢╕+ р╢║ р╖Др╖Р=8 =р╢║р╢▒ р╢Ср╢Ъ" р╖Гр╢│р╖Д р╢Ър╢╗р╢▒р╢з р╢Ър╖Рр╢╕р╖РU8. р╢Т р╢Еlр╖А A# р╢вр╖ПUр╢Ъ р╖Ар╖Рр╢й Cр╖Щр╖Ар╖Еe |р╢║р╖П"р╢╕р╢Ъ р╖Щр╢Ър╢з р╖Щр╢╕р╢╕ р╢н""р╖Ар╢║ р╢┤р╖Пр╢╜р╢▒р╢║ =zр╢╕р╢з р╢Ер╖Ар╖Б( р╢║р╖Ар╢╗ р╢Ьр╢н d+ р╢║р╖Р8 р╢Е р╖Щр╢║р╢вр╢▒р╖П р╢Ър╢╗р╢▒р╖Ар╖П.

р╖Щр╢╕р╢╕ р╢┤$┬╣р╢╕ р╢║р╢зр╖Щ" р╢вр╖ПUр╢Ъ р╖Ар╖Рр╢пр╢Ь"р╢Ър╢╕= d" р╢Ъ_р╢лe р╖Ар╖Бр╖Щр╢║ р╖Гр╢╜р╢Ър╖П, р╢┤р╖Др╢н р╢Ъ_x Cр╢╢р╢│р╖А р╢╗р╢вр╖Щр╢║ Aр╖Бр╖К┬Тр╢н C+_ р╖Др╖П р╢┤р╖Рр╖Др╖Р4y =z. р╢╢р╢╜р╖Пр╖Щр╢┤р╖Щр╢╗"+ р╖Щр╖А^.

1) р╖Щ. р╖Ар╢▒ р╢з р╢╗р╖Щp -Uр╖ЩJ р╢Жр╢┤р╢н(р╢║ ┬╣р╢│ р╖Ар╖Р┬┤ р╢ЗU р╢╢р╖А", р╢Ър╖Пр╢нр╖Пр╖Ар╢з р╖Др╖П р╢п_р╖Ар╢з ┬╣р╖Щр╢║ р╖Гр╖Рр╖Щр╢Ъ р╖Щр╢нр╢╗р╖А Aр╢пр╖Др╖Щр╖Гk ┬пр╖А"sр╖Щ. р╢Ер╖Ар╖Гр╖Кр╢ор╖Пр╖А р╢Е┬Г^ s р╖Щр╢Ьр╖Гр╖К р╢ЗU р╢╢р╖А", р╢Ср╢║ р╖А:р╢нр╢╕р╖Пр╢▒ р╢╗р╢вр╖ЩJ р╢┤2р╢┤р╖Пр╢╜р╢▒ o:р╖Ар╢╜р╢нр╖Пр╖Щ0 GUр╢╡р╢╜р╢║e р╢╢р╖А" р╢╗р╢вр╢║ Cр╢Ьр╖Щр╢п? р╖Щр╢▒р╢Ср╖Щр╖Гk р╢▒. р╢Т р╢╕р╢п?

р╢Ь6 р╢Ър╢ор╖Пр╢▒р╖Пр╢║р╢Ъ5р╢╕р╖П (рооро╛ рооро┐ роЪрокро╛роиро╛ропроХ роЕро╡роХ) (The Hon. Speaker) Next, there is a Question of Privilege to be raised by the Hon. M.A. Sumanthiran. р╖Ар╢╗0р╖Гр╖Пр╢п: 2020 р╖Щр╢┤р╢╢р╢╗р╖Ар╖П 16 [р╢▒ "р╖Г?р╖Щ┬Ч р╢Еeр╢╜?┬Ч" р╖Ар╖П р╢нр╖Пр╖А роЪро┐ро▒ро╛ро┐рпИроо: 2020 рпЖрокро╡ро╛ро┐ 16роЖ рпЗродродро┐роп тАЬроЪ рпЗроЯ роРро▓ "тАЭ роЕро▒ро┐$рпИроХ PRIVILEGE: "SUNDAY ISLAND" REPORT OF 16TH FEBRUARY, 2020 р╢Ь6 р╢С<.р╢Т. Aр╢╕?р╢╗? р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П (рооро╛ рооро┐ роО.роП. :рооCродро┐ро░) (The Hon. M.A. Sumanthiran) Thank you, Hon. Speaker, for permitting me to raise this issue today.

I refer to an article published on page 13 of тАЬSunday IslandтАЭ of 16th, February, 2020 by one C.A. Chandraprema, titled тАЬPolitics of the High Posts Committee of Parliament". Sir, I table* a copy of that newspaper article.

Mr. Chandraprema is a nominee for the post of Permanent Representative of Sri Lanka to the United Nations in Geneva. This article, in its entirety, violates the Privilege not only of myself as a Member of Parliament, but also of the Committee on High Posts and of the whole Parliament itself.

While it is wholly improper for him to have written this article while he was awaiting clearance by the Committee on High Posts, the irony is that he speaks of a conflict of interest. I do not know this Chandraprema personally and I have only heard of him in relation to his writings. He claims that some people have made allegations that he was part of a death squad that carried out extrajudicial killings. Having put the cap on, so to say, he does not even deny these allegations in his article, but merely says that one must ask the former Prime Minister whether he was ordered to carry out these killings, which include three lawyers.

I state that this article breaches the Privilege of this House and urge you, Mr. Speaker, to take appropriate action against the said Chandraprema and the said newspaper. I also wish to draw the attention of the Hon. Minister of Foreign Relations, who is present in the House at the moment, with regard to this nomination of Mr. C.A. Chandraprema of all places to Geneva.

Thank you.

It was not an investigation initiated by the Central Bank or the COPE. That came into being because of the recommendations of the Presidential Commission of Inquiry, which was initiated by President Maithripala Sirisena at that time.

The five Forensic Reports are the outcome of that investigation, which were recently tabled in Parliament and have been debated on the Floor of this House for two full days. I am deeply surprised that responsible Members of Parliament and responsible Ministers of the Government are reading out the legalistic jargon in those Reports, which is always there in all such reports, to say that even those Reports say that this is not correct. No. In fact, these Forensic Audit Reports have been done by two of the best expert forensic companies chosen after careful scrutiny. These reports actually reveal so much about corruption in this country in the last 20 years and that is why, after one full day's Debate, the Hon. (Dr.) Bandula Gunawardane and other irresponsible Members of this Government are now trying to sabotage even the Debate and stop us from debating and telling the country what is really there.

Sir, due to the limited time allotted to me, then I will touch on Report No. 3, which sets out in detail how the mafia family and friends pillaged the EmployeesтАЩ Provident Fund. Perhaps, I should use the word тАЬplunderтАЭ, plundering of workersтАЩ funds. Or even better, if I have the way, I will name this final Report by the KPMG, India on the EPF robbery as the тАЬRape of the EmployeesтАЩ Provident FundтАЭ. The EmployeesтАЩ Provident Fund had been raped systematically over the five years and it had been done by, as I said, a network of family and friends of the then Government. In fact, in this Report, there is a family tree. This is not some political concoction.

This has been done by the company. This was the pump-and-dump policy of the then Government. Again, I am quoting very quickly from this Report:

"2. Key breaches occurred in the following:

Investigation revealed that various activities in EPF, including investment in trading or investment portfolio were performed without express approvals or mandate in the IPS/ITG. Key deviations that were noted are:

- Portfolio level breaches and breach of individual security limit and trading limit.

- Investment transactions without IC/MB approval.

- Deviation from IC plan for execution of transactions.

- Irregularities in addition of companies to the ASL.

- Investments made without adequate analysis.

- Unsigned deal tickets and settlement sheets.

- Investment in unlisted equity without express provisions in IPS/ITG and approval of Monetary Board (e.g. investment of LKR 500 million in Sri Lankan Airlines in 2010, investment of LKR 1000 million for Sri Lankan Catering).

- Investment of LKR 1539.44 million in five banking shares based on instructions/approval from the Governor during 2009 and 2010.тАЭ

So, as I said, these five Reports actually warrant at least five days of debate in this House. This is one of the most shocking revelations the country has ever seen. That is why I say again that this Report should be named the тАЬRape of the EPFтАЭ because it shows how the money of the poor working people of this country was systematically robbed, pillaged and plundered during the period when the then Governor Mr. Ajith Nivard Cabraal was in charge.

Therefore, like in all other things, let us not debate this in the House, forget about it and then allow the same things to continue happening, perhaps at an even faster pace in the future. I think rather than taking sides and trying to justify oneтАЩs own side, it is time that the country, as a whole, as the Hon. Anura Dissanayake said, get together at least now to ensure that such daylight robbery of public assets do not take place in the future.

Thank you. р╢Ь6 _р╖Щр╢║Pр╢в] р╢Ър╢ор╖Пр╢▒р╖Пр╢║р╢Ъ5р╢╕р╖П (рооро╛ рооро┐ рокро┐ро░родро┐2 роЪрокро╛роиро╛ропроХ роЕро╡роХ) (The Hon. That is the problem. When there is no transparency, you do not know whether it is right or wrong.

661 662

[р╢Ь_ р╢╜р╖Гр╢н р╢Ер╢╜wр╢║р╖Ар╢▒ р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П]

2020 р╖Щр╢┤р╢╢р╢╗р╖Ар╖П2 19

р╢Ь6 р╢╗ р╖Жр╖К р╖Дa< р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П (рооро╛ рооро┐ ро▒1? ро╣роХрпА) (The Hon. Rauff Hakeem) Madam Presiding Member, I was referring to the particular Forensic Audit Reports pointing out glaring deficiencies relating to prudence, governance, accountability and transparency when it comes to Bond issues in this country.

Madam Presiding Member, my humble request to this august Assembly is to act with responsibility as Representatives of citizens instead of trading accusations across the aisle and let us all collectively work towards ensuring that such blatant abuses of power and positions are not repeated. Now, it is a matter of pot calling the kettle black. That is what we have been witnessing these two days.

Whilst leaving the technicalities contained in the Report to be debated by professionals with competence, I will limit my address to purely focus on conclusions in the Report solely related to the role of the Central Bank of Sri Lanka, the Governor, the Monetary Board and lastly, the Employees' Provident Fund, Sri Lanka's largest social security fund which manages the general public's social security contributions.

Before I proceed further with my limited address on the identified areas, I wish to highlight to this august Assembly two glaring deficiencies in the Report. That is, two vital areas the Reports have not addressed and which deserve to be addressed. The first being the role of the State banks in the two tainted auctions related to the alleged Bond Scam, from the Report, it is evident that the State banks have consistently been the biggest source of liquidity providers to Government Bonds.

The Reports have failed not only to identify the causes for the State banks not participating in the two tainted auctions, but also to identify support for any justification provided for the absence of the State banks at these auctions. Based on views expressed by market participants, non-participation of the State banks was the biggest contributor in the execution of this outright scam through the two tainted auctions. Market participants are strongly of the view that the State banks, if they had participated, would have scooped up a big majority of the Bonds offered in the two tainted issues at much lower yields, close to market yields, thus preventing or significantly reducing the loss suffered by the Government through these two issues. To date, there is no justifiable basis or answers to support the non-participation of the State banks.

Madam Presiding Member, the second point is the loss caused to the general public because of the sharp spike in yield rates after the two tainted auctions. Several attempts have been made to compute the loss suffered by the Government, but no attempt has been made to date to compute the secondary market loss suffered by the general public who were holding bonds and who were forced to sell due to the artificial spike in the market yield, which resulted in margin calls by banks on their leveraged positions. The question that needs answers in

relation to this is, which primary dealer scooped up all these Bonds from the secondary market and were those also sold to the EPF later on when rates stabilized? Madam Presiding Member, I am of the firm view that the general public deserves answers to these two questions.

Coming back to the subject of my address, what is glaringly evident from the Reports is the callous manner the individuals politically exposed to the Government of the day, whether it be the previous Government, the last Government or the present rulers, have blatantly gone about manipulating the orderly working of the Central Bank by influencing the highest officers of the Central Bank to enrich a selected group of individuals at a great cost to the general public.

Every officer working for or holding post in the institutions identified, namely the Central Bank, the Governor, the Monetary Board and the EmployeesтАЩ Provident Fund, is a fiduciary. A fiduciary is legally defined as тАЬa relationship in trust, especially in relation to the trustee and the beneficiariesтАЭ. In the said instant, the institutions identified are trustees of the citizens, who are the beneficiaries. The duty of a fiduciary entails the highest standard of care in equity or law towards the beneficiaries, to whom the duty is owed. The highest standard of care requires a fiduciary to act prudently with due skill, care, diligence and judgement in relation to the affairs of the beneficiaries. Madam Presiding Member, the persons identified in the Forensic Audit Reports related to the institutions that I have highlighted are all professionals entrusted with trust under a fiduciary relationship, who owe a fiduciary duty to the general public, purportedly with competence to administer and manage monies belonging to the people of this country; in this instant, the Central BankтАЩs monies and the beneficiaries of the EmployeesтАЩ Provident Fund.

This House should also take due note of the fact that in relation to administration and management of public monies, globally the bar set for prudence in relation to fiduciary duties is at a very high level. Coming back to the conclusions in the Reports, this august Assembly should take due note that, leave alone the prudent rule, even basic rules of prudence through average skill, care, diligence and judgement have been alien not only to the individuals identified in the Report, but also to those at the Central Bank, the institution entrusted with statutory responsibility to maintain economic and price stability and financial stability as an institution that enforces rules of prudence in the financial sector in the country and the EmployeesтАЩ Provident Fund, a statutory body set up to manage a social security scheme, which is managed by the Central Bank.

This, Madam Presiding Member, is a very sad state of affairs for the country in general and the people in particular. Why did the Central Bank of Sri Lanka, which had, which has and which will have in the future the cream of high standard professionals with eminence stoop to such a low level? The Central Bank of Sri Lanka stooping to such a low level is a higher economic cost to the people of Sri Lanka than the financial loss everyone is attempting to compute through allegations across the

663 664

р╢┤р╖П:yр╖Щ.+р╖А

aisle. Yes, the financial losses being computed is very significant, but the economic cost of allowing the Central Bank to continue in its current state far outweighs that cost.

Madam Presiding Member, I would like to once again ask this House the question, who is responsible for this current state of affairs? I will have to humbly admit that every Hon. Member of this House including you, Madam, the Speaker, myself, and everyone across the divide, is collectively responsible for the current state of the Central Bank. We, as Legislators, have failed in our duty to bring reforms to the Central Bank in line with the transformations taking place globally. Our age-old legislations are a stumbling block for the Central Bank to achieve the high standards that this nation expects and deserves from such an august institution.

From the Forensic Audit Reports, it is blatantly evident that the culprits behind the Central Bank being pushed to such a low level are the politically exposed and aligned persons associated with the running of the Central Bank. Madam Presiding Member, if we do not act now, future legislators will once again be wasting the time of this Legislature, trying to unravel another calamity, potentially of a higher magnitude, at enormous cost to the people of this nation. The answer to this puzzle is the independence of the Central Bank; the Central Bank should be made constitutionally independent and autonomous in order to ensure that it is totally devoid of political influence. A Central Bank cannot be run by politically affiliated individuals whose decisions will always be biased towards their political masters and aligned towards agendas with vested interest. The Forensic Audit Reports provide sufficient evidence to support this conclusion. Therefore, we can go on pontificating until the kingdom come, but we will not see the dawn unless we act now.

Madam Presiding Member, every Hon. Member of this august Assembly has a bounden duty to act now and make our Central Bank a constitutionally independent institution, an institution devoid of political influence. It is time for all of us to put aside political differences and for once, act in the interest of our nation and make our Central Bank an independent, autonomous institution.

Coming to the subject of the EmployeesтАЩ Provident Fund, the EPF is entrusted with statutory responsibility to manage Sri LankaтАЩs largest social security scheme. The EPF manages assets in excess of Rs. 2.2 trillion as at December, 2018. To put it into perspective, this translates to US Dollars 12.8 billion or close to 15 per cent of Sri LankaтАЩs GDP, Gross Domestic Product! The Central Bank is entrusted with the responsibility of managing this humongous asset base on behalf of the general public, the majority being the private sector employees. The EPF is another institution which owes a fiduciary duty to the general public. The time is right for EPF to be managed independently devoid of political influence by a Board of Governors consisting of officials from the Treasury, the Central Bank and the private sector with a professional

management team with fund management experience in place, similar to how pension funds are managed globally. It should be strictly governed by an investment mandate and the performance should be linked to clearly defined benchmarks. Potentially, the management team could be incentivized for overperforming over a hurdle rate as a benchmark, similar to how pension fund managers are incentivized globally. This will enable the EPF not only to be efficiently managed, but also to provide beneficiaries a better return. In evaluating the EPFтАЩs performance over the last 10 years, it is evident the EPF have been providing beneficiaries a return very close to the long-term government bond yields. These beneficiaries, at the time of encashing these assets, are liable for tax and the tax adjusted return received by these beneficiaries would be less than the return they would have got, if they themselves invested these monies in long-term Government Bonds, and the interest income related to which is not liable for tax.

Madam, the question I want to pose is, what is the benefit to the beneficiary from an independent institution managing its social security assets at a large cost to the beneficiary, if that institution is to provide a return less than the return the beneficiaries could have generated on their own? Therefore, I also want to pose the question, is the EPF really set up for the benefit of the beneficiaries or is it a mechanism for persons with political affiliations to benefit in the guise of providing benefits to the beneficiaries?

Sri LankaтАЩs private sector is on par with their global counterparts and the big players who are listed operate efficiently within a regulated environment - look at our blue-chip companies - within a transparent and accountable regime, whilst generating and creating value to their shareholders. This segment of the private sector has not only professional expertise, but also access to a transparent and accountable framework devoid of political influence and affiliations to administer and manage an operation like the Employees' Provident Fund within a governance-based, transparent and accountable framework under a competent Board of Governors.

Therefore, Madam Presiding Member, the question I want to pose to all of us is, should we continue to permit politically affiliated individuals to callously profit out of Sri Lanka's largest social security scheme - this pumping-and- dumping operation, how long are we to tolerate? - and deprive the beneficiaries of a return they deserve or should the EPF be reformed through the legislative structure by this House to put in place mechanisms for the EPF to be managed by a professional management team under the aegis of a professional Board of Governors with a governance-based, transparent and accountable framework? That is the question I would like to pose. Therefore, it is time that we look at in a non-partisan manner and devise methods to make the Central Bank an independent, autonomous institution.

Though the autonomy has been guaranteed by various legislations, continuous political meddling has messed up the entire scene. The confidence in our main watchdog when it comes to monetary policy has also been affected

665 666

[р╢Ь_ р╢╗┬Ьр╖Жр╖К р╖Дb. р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П]

2020 р╖Щр╢┤р╢╢р╢╗р╖Ар╖П2 19

due to this continuous and relentless bond scams that are being allowed to perpetuate the climate for profiteering by various unscrupulous elements. Therefore, it is time for us to take stock of these Forensic Audit Reports and take legal action against all those who were involved and also see that these two institutions are managed with much better professional management with a better legislation in place.

Thank you.

Madam Chair, issuance of licences for brokerages is also a serious issue. There has to be a mechanism which enables an independent body to look into the issuance of licences for brokerages.

Licences for brokerages issue р╢Ър╢╗р╢╜р╖П Uр╖Щр╢╢р╢▒ р╢Жр╢Ър╖Пр╢╗р╢║ 4р╖Др╖П р╢╢р╢╜р╢▒ р╖Щр╢Ър╢з р╖Щр╢┤р╖Щр╢▒р╢▒р╖Ар╖П, $oр╖Гр╖Кр╖Г Cр╢╢р╢│ р╢нр╢╗р╖ПUр╢╗р╢╕e р╢╢р╢╜р╖Щ р╢▒р╖РUр╖А р╢Тр╢Ъ" р╖Щр╢╢р╢пр╢╜р╖П Uр╖Щр╢╢р╖Щ р╖Щhр╖Бр╢┤р╖Пр╢╜р╢▒ ^+р╢╗р╢з8 - р╢║р╖П┬Кр╖Ар╢з8 - =р╢║р╢▒ р╢Ър╖Пр╢╗р╢лр╢║. Therefore, we have to introduce a mechanism; there should be a mechanism to issue licences for brokerages. Also, there is an officials' mafia.

It being 6.30 p.m., THE HON. PRESIDING MEMBER adjourned Parliament without Question put. Parliament adjourned accordingly until 9.30 a.m. on Thursday, 20th February, 2020, pursuant to the Resolution of Parliament of this Day.
